## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: The task describes a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, with dv/dt (acceleration) as target and t (time) and v (velocity) as features. In such systems, acceleration can depend on velocity through damping (linear or nonlinear) and on time via external driving forces, or can be expressed purely in terms of velocity if the system is conservative (using energy conservation to eliminate displacement).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear unforced damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v
- Linear damping with constant forcing: dv_dt = c0 - c1 * v
- Quadratic turbulent drag: dv_dt = -c0 * v * Abs(v)
- Cubic nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v**3
- Conservative harmonic oscillator (energy conservation): dv_dt = c0 * Sqrt(c1 - c2 * v**2)
- Conservative anharmonic oscillator (quartic potential): dv_dt = c0 * Sqrt(c1 - c2 * v**2 - c3 * v**4)
- Linear damping with sinusoidal driving: dv_dt = c0 * Sin(c1 * t + c2) - c3 * v
- Cubic damping with sinusoidal driving: dv_dt = c0 * Cos(c1 * t) - c2 * v - c3 * v**3
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * Cos(c2 * t)) * v
- Harmonic oscillator phase relation: dv_dt = c0 * v / Tan(c1 * t + c2)
- Nonlinear drag with square-root: dv_dt = -c0 * Sign(v) * Sqrt(Abs(v))
- Rayleigh-type damping: dv_dt = c0 * v * (c1 - v**2)
- Time-dependent damping: dv_dt = c0 * t * v + c1 * v

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- In conservative oscillators, acceleration depends only on velocity through energy conservation, often involving sqrt of a quadratic or quartic polynomial in v.
- For forced oscillators, acceleration contains an additive periodic term in t (e.g., sin or cos) representing the external drive.
- Nonlinear damping introduces terms like -c*v**3 or -c*Abs(v)*v in the acceleration equation.
- In a simple harmonic oscillator, the exact phase relationship yields acceleration proportional to v divided by tan(ωt+φ).
- Anharmonic or Duffing oscillators lead to higher-order polynomials of v when displacement is eliminated via energy conservation.
- Parametric resonance can appear as a product of velocity and a periodic function of time.
- Combined damping and driving typically sum a decay term (proportional to v) and a time-dependent driving force.
- Velocity-dependent drag with a fractional power (e.g., sqrt) indicates non-Newtonian or turbulent fluid damping.
